governments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMycockHayton2014265_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMycockHayton2014265-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> In its 2015 manifesto, it promised to make <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="St. George&#39;s Day">St. George's Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._David%27s_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="St. David&#39;s Day">St. David's Day</a> <a href="/wiki/Bank_holiday" title="Bank holiday">bank holidays</a> in England and Wales, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayton2016403_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayton2016403-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, UKIP's 2017 manifesto pledged to declare 23 June British Independence Day and observe it annually as a <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">national holiday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Euroscepticism.2C_immigration_and_foreign_policy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Euroscepticism,_immigration_and_foreign_policy">Euroscepticism, immigration and foreign policy</span></h3>
<p>UKIP embraces the ideology of <a href="/wiki/Hard_Euroscepticism" class="mw-redirect" title="Hard Euroscepticism">hard Euroscepticism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynchWhitakerLoomes2012733Tournier-Sol2015141–42Dye20157_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynchWhitakerLoomes2012733Tournier-Sol2015141–42Dye20157-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> also known as "Eurorejectionism".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDye20157_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDye20157-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Opposition to the United Kingdom's continued membership of the European Union has been its "core issue" and is "central to the party's identity".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014193,_195_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014193,_195-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> UKIP characterises the EU as a fundamentally undemocratic institution and stresses the need to regain what it describes as the UK's <a href="/wiki/Westphalian_sovereignty" title="Westphalian sovereignty">national sovereignty</a> from the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015142_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015142-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> It presents the EU as being an exemplar of non-accountability, corruption, and inefficiency, and views it as being responsible for the "flooding" of the UK with migrants, in particular from Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016173_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016173-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> UKIP emphasises Euroscepticism to a far greater extent than any of Western Europe's other main radical right parties,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014187–88_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014187–88-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> and it was only post-2010 that it began seriously articulating other issues.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014233_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014233-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Hayton nevertheless suggested that Euroscepticism still remains "the lens through which most of its other policy positions are framed and understood".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayton2016400_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayton2016400-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Starcross_,_The_Strand,_UKIP_Poster_and_Starcross_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345072.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Starcross_%2C_The_Strand%2C_UKIP_Poster_and_Starcross_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345072.jpg/220px-Starcross_%2C_The_Strand%2C_UKIP_Poster_and_Starcross_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345072.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Starcross_%2C_The_Strand%2C_UKIP_Poster_and_Starcross_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345072.jpg/330px-Starcross_%2C_The_Strand%2C_UKIP_Poster_and_Starcross_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345072.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Starcross_%2C_The_Strand%2C_UKIP_Poster_and_Starcross_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345072.jpg/440px-Starcross_%2C_The_Strand%2C_UKIP_Poster_and_Starcross_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345072.jpg 2x" data-file-width="492" data-file-height="305" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Starcross_,_The_Strand,_UKIP_Poster_and_Starcross_Sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345072.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UKIP placard on the side of the road in <a href="/wiki/Starcross" title="Starcross">Starcross</a>, Devon, declaring: "Say NO to European Union"</div></div></div>
<p>The party opposed the <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">2004 enlargement of the European Union</a> into eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEtheridge201414_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEtheridge201414-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> UKIP advocated leaving the European Union, stopping payments to the EU, and withdrawing from <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">EU treaties</a>, while maintaining trading ties with other European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Local_elections:_What_does_UKIP_stand_for?_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Local_elections:_What_does_UKIP_stand_for?-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Initially, UKIP's policy was that, in the event of them winning a general election, it would remove the UK from the EU without a referendum on the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2016a28_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2016a28-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The party leadership later suggested a referendum, expressing the view that in the case of an exit vote, it could negotiate favourable terms for the country's withdrawal, for instance through ensuring a <a href="/wiki/Free_trade_agreement" title="Free trade agreement">free trade agreement</a> between the UK and EU.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynchWhitakerLoomes2012741_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynchWhitakerLoomes2012741-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> UKIP eventually committed to a referendum in their 2015 manifesto.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2016a28_96-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2016a28-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In contrast to involvement in the EU, UKIP has emphasised the UK's global connections, in particularly to member states of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015144_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015144-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> UKIP rejected the description that they were "Europhobes", maintaining that its stance was anti-EU, not anti-European.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015144_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015144-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UKIP has placed great emphasis on the issue of immigration to the UK,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynchWhitakerLoomes2012754Tournier-Sol2015146_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynchWhitakerLoomes2012754Tournier-Sol2015146-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> and in 2013 Farage described it as "the biggest single issue facing this party".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015146_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015146-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> UKIP attributes UK membership of the EU as the core cause of immigration to the UK, citing the Union's open-border policies as the reason why large numbers of East European migrants have moved to Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015146_187-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015146-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> On their campaign billboards, UKIP have presented EU migrants as a source of crime, as well as a pressure on housing, the welfare state, and the health service.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201542_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201542-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Farage has emphasised not only the economic impact of migration but also the public anxieties regarding the cultural changes brought by immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201542_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201542-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> In its 2009 electoral manifesto, UKIP proposed a five-year ban on any migrants coming to the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016173_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016173-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> By 2015, it had modified this to the view that the five-year ban should apply only to unskilled migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015231_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015231-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> To regulate the arrival of skilled migrants, it called for the UK to adopt a points-based system akin to that employed by Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015172,_231Heywood2015139_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015172,_231Heywood2015139-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> It advocated the establishment of a watchdog to help curb immigration, and bring the levels of net annual immigration down from the hundreds of thousands to between 20,000 and 50,000, which was the average level in the UK between 1950 and 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015231_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015231-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> UKIP calls for all immigrants to require compulsory health insurance,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015231_189-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015231-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> and proposes that migrants be barred from claiming any state benefits until they had been resident in the UK for at least five years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016183_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016183-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Exeter_,_Cowley_Bridge_Road_and_UKIP_Hoarding_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345943.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Exeter_%2C_Cowley_Bridge_Road_and_UKIP_Hoarding_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345943.jpg/220px-Exeter_%2C_Cowley_Bridge_Road_and_UKIP_Hoarding_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345943.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Exeter_%2C_Cowley_Bridge_Road_and_UKIP_Hoarding_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345943.jpg/330px-Exeter_%2C_Cowley_Bridge_Road_and_UKIP_Hoarding_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345943.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Exeter_%2C_Cowley_Bridge_Road_and_UKIP_Hoarding_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345943.jpg/440px-Exeter_%2C_Cowley_Bridge_Road_and_UKIP_Hoarding_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345943.jpg 2x" data-file-width="520" data-file-height="356" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Exeter_,_Cowley_Bridge_Road_and_UKIP_Hoarding_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1345943.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UKIP poster in <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a> in 2009: "Say NO to Unlimited Immigration"</div></div></div>
<p>UKIP gained traction from the fact that post-2008, immigration had come to the forefront of many Britons' minds as a result of increased EU migration and its concomitant social changes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201528–30_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201528–30-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> By the 2015 general election, the political scientists James Dennison and Matthew Goodwin argued, UKIP had secured "ownership" of the immigration issue among British voters, having secured it from the Conservatives.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015169,_179_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015169,_179-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> However, the party's campaign against immigration has been accused of using racism and xenophobia to win votes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201543_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201543-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Political scientist David Art suggested that in its campaign to restrict immigration, UKIP had "flirted with xenophobia",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArt2011104_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArt2011104-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> while Daniel T. Dye stated that part of the party's appeal was its "sometimes-xenophobic populism",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDye20152_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDye20152-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> and the journalist <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Trilling" title="Daniel Trilling">Daniel Trilling</a> stated that UKIP tapped into the "anti-immigrant and anti-Muslim populism" that was popular in the late 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrilling2012154_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrilling2012154-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> The political scientist Simon Usherwood stated that UKIP's hardening of immigration policy "risked reinforcing the party's profile as a quasi-far-right grouping",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2008258_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2008258-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> elsewhere stating that the party was only held together by its opposition to the EU and immigration, suggesting that it had "no ideological coherence" beyond that.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2016a29_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2016a29-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In its 2015 campaign, UKIP called for the foreign aid budget to be cut.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015238_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015238-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> It has also advocated a 40% increase in the UK's national defence budget.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015146_187-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015146-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> It opposes UK military involvement in conflicts that are not perceived to be in the national interest, specifically rejecting the concept of <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_intervention" title="Humanitarian intervention">humanitarian interventionism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015146_187-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015146-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> For instance, in 2014 it opposed the Cameron government's plans to intervene militarily against the government of <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_civil_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian civil war">Syrian civil war</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin201496Tournier-Sol2015146_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin201496Tournier-Sol2015146-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, UKIP pledged to work with anti-EU populist group <a href="/wiki/The_Movement_(populist_group)" title="The Movement (populist group)">The Movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_policy">Economic policy</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25em;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"So what kind of party is UKIP? Ideologically, the party combines a mix of old-style liberal commitments to free markets, limited government and individual freedom with conservative appeals to national sovereignty and traditional social values."</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— Political scientist Stephen Driver, 2011<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDriver2011147_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDriver2011147-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>On economic policy, UKIP shares the main three parties' acceptance of the core principles of a capitalist market economy,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinlowHallTreadwell201744_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinlowHallTreadwell201744-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> and the party is generally at ease with the global <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin20147_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin20147-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> The academics Simon Winlow, Steve Hall, and James Treadwell commented that on economic issues, "UKIP wants to have its cake and eat it. It wants to retain the best bits of the market economy while discarding what it considers the negative outcomes of 21st-century neoliberalism."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinlowHallTreadwell201743–44_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinlowHallTreadwell201743–44-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> They noted for instance that it wanted "free movement of capital" yet wanted to curtail "the free movement of workers across borders".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinlowHallTreadwell201743_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinlowHallTreadwell201743-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On economic issues, UKIP's original activist base was largely <a href="/wiki/Libertarianism" title="Libertarianism">libertarian</a>, supporting an <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">economically liberal</a> approach.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014277_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014277-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Its libertarian views have been influenced by <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">classical liberalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thatcherism" title="Thatcherism">Thatcherism</a>, with Thatcher representing a key influence on UKIP's thought.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015145_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015145-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Farage has characterised UKIP as "the true inheritors" of Thatcher, claiming that the party never would have formed had Thatcher remained Prime Minister of the UK throughout the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015145_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015145-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Winlow, Hall, and Treadwell suggested that a UKIP government would pursue "hard-core Thatcherism" on economic policy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinlowHallTreadwell201743_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinlowHallTreadwell201743-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> UKIP presents itself as a libertarian party,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin20147Tournier-Sol2015145LynchWhitaker2013296_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin20147Tournier-Sol2015145LynchWhitaker2013296-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> and the political scientists David Deacon and Dominic Wring described it as articulating "a potent brand of libertarian populism".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016170_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016170-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> However, commentators writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spectator" title="The Spectator">The Spectator</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/New_Statesman" title="New Statesman">New Statesman</a></i> have all challenged the description of UKIP as libertarian, highlighting its socially conservative and economically <a href="/wiki/Protectionist" class="mw-redirect" title="Protectionist">protectionist</a> policies as being contrary to a libertarian ethos.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UKIP propose an increase in the <a href="/wiki/Personal_allowance" title="Personal allowance">personal allowance</a> to the level of full-time <a href="/wiki/National_Minimum_Wage_Act_1998" title="National Minimum Wage Act 1998">minimum wage</a> earnings (approx. £13,500 as of the 2015 General Election). It also plans to abolish <a href="/wiki/Inheritance_Tax_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Inheritance Tax (United Kingdom)">Inheritance Tax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
It would introduce a 35p income tax rate for taxable income between £42,285 and £55,000, with the 40p rate payable above that.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> UKIP would allow businesses to favour British workers over migrants,<sup id="cite_ref-wilfully_misinterpreted_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wilfully_misinterpreted-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> and would repeal "much of" Britain's racial discrimination law, which was described as "shocking" by the <a href="/wiki/Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition" title="Cameron–Clegg coalition">Conservative–Liberal Democrat coalition government</a><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> and viewed as discriminatory by others.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> However, Farage insists that his comments regarding his party's policies on these matters have been "wilfully misinterpreted".<sup id="cite_ref-wilfully_misinterpreted_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wilfully_misinterpreted-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
Although the party does not have an official stance on the <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_Trade_and_Investment_Partnership" title="Transatlantic Trade and Investment Partnership">Transatlantic Trade and Investment Partnership</a>, the party's former international trade spokesperson (<a href="/wiki/William_Legge,_10th_Earl_of_Dartmouth" title="William Legge, 10th Earl of Dartmouth">Lord Dartmouth</a>) and former health and social care spokesperson (<a href="/wiki/Louise_Bours" title="Louise Bours">Louise Bours</a>) have stated that they do not wish the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">National Health Service</a> to be included in the trade deal, according to the <i><a href="/wiki/International_Business_Times" title="International Business Times">International Business Times</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_policy">Social policy</span></h3>
<p>On health, UKIP's policy is to keep the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">National Health Service</a> and general practitioner visits free at the point of use for UK citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015134_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015134-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> Non-citizens would be required to have approved medical insurance "as a condition of entering the UK".<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Farage attracted widespread press attention for suggesting that HIV positive patients who were not UK citizens should not receive treatment on the NHS.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015168_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015168-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> In that same speech he stated that the UK should put the NHS "there for British people and families, who in many cases have paid into the system for years".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015168_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennisonGoodwin2015168-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> Farage has spoken in favour of an insurance-based system in the past, which he said would resemble the French and Dutch style system rather than an American style private system, but this was rejected by the party. He has commented, "we may have to think about ways in the future about dealing with health care differently".<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Critics of UKIP have claimed that the party's real desire is to dismantle and <a href="/wiki/Privatisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Privatisation">privatise</a> the NHS,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015134_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015134-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> a claim bolstered by the publication of leaked documents showing that in 2013 the UKIP NEC privately spoke positively of NHS privatisation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015220_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015220-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ukipppc2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ukipppc2010.jpg/220px-Ukipppc2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ukipppc2010.jpg/330px-Ukipppc2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ukipppc2010.jpg/440px-Ukipppc2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="1880" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ukipppc2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A UKIP candidate campaigning in the run-up to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2010 United Kingdom general election">2010 general election</a></div></div></div>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, commentator Ed Rooksby described UKIP's approach to many social issues as being "traditionalist and socially conservative",<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> while political scientist Stephen Driver has referred to the party's appeals to "traditional social values".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDriver2011147_202-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDriver2011147-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> UKIP opposed the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Same-sex marriage in the United Kingdom">same-sex marriage in the United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClements2014242Tournier-Sol2015146_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClements2014242Tournier-Sol2015146-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> UKIP wants to repeal the <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Act_1998" title="Human Rights Act 1998">Human Rights Act</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbediLundberg200973_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbediLundberg200973-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> and remove Britain from both the European Convention on Refugees and the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a> (ECHR).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEtheridge201442–43_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEtheridge201442–43-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Immigration_policy_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immigration_policy-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> On the repeal of Britain's signatory to the ECHR, UKIP would like to see a referendum on the reintroduction of the <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Capital punishment in the United Kingdom">death penalty in the UK</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEtheridge201443_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEtheridge201443-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although Farage had long been reticent about focusing on public anxieties surrounding Muslims in Britain, he spoke out following the <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Hebdo_shooting" title="Charlie Hebdo shooting"><i>Charlie Hebdo</i> shooting</a>, claiming that there was a "fifth column" of Islamists in the UK who—while "mercifully small" in number—were "out to destroy our whole civilisation".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015214_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015214-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> At the same time he called for Western states to do more to promote their <a href="/wiki/Judeo-Christian" title="Judeo-Christian">Judeo-Christian</a> heritage,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015214_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015214-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> and criticised state <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multiculturalism</a> for promoting social segregation, discouraging integration, and generating a "tick-box approach" to <a href="/wiki/Identity_politics" title="Identity politics">identity politics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015214_230-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015214-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> In its 2017 manifesto, UKIP pledged to abolish the existence of <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">sharia courts</a> in the UK and ban the wearing of the <a href="/wiki/Niqab" class="mw-redirect" title="Niqab">niqab</a> and burka in public; it claimed that these were needed to promote the integration of Muslims with wider British society.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UKIP is the only major political party in the United Kingdom that does not endorse <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> and lower carbon emissions,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReed2016229_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReed2016229-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> and its media output regularly promotes <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_denial" title="Climate change denial">climate change denial</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReed2016237_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReed2016237-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Farage and other senior UKIP figures have repeatedly spoken out against the construction of <a href="/wiki/Wind_farms" class="mw-redirect" title="Wind farms">wind farms</a>, deeming them a blot on the rural landscape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReed2016233–36_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReed2016233–36-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> UKIP's media present renewable energy as inefficient and unaffordable,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReed2016237_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReed2016237-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> and they promote the use of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear energy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fracking" class="mw-redirect" title="Fracking">fracking</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReed2016238_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReed2016238-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
UKIP has announced that it would repeal the <a href="/wiki/Climate_Change_Act_2008" title="Climate Change Act 2008">Climate Change Act 2008</a> and has placed an emphasis on protecting the <a href="/wiki/Green_belt_(United_Kingdom)" title="Green belt (United Kingdom)">Green Belt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UKIP_poster_in_Alexandra_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1362476.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/UKIP_poster_in_Alexandra_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1362476.jpg/170px-UKIP_poster_in_Alexandra_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1362476.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/UKIP_poster_in_Alexandra_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1362476.jpg/255px-UKIP_poster_in_Alexandra_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1362476.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/UKIP_poster_in_Alexandra_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1362476.jpg/340px-UKIP_poster_in_Alexandra_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1362476.jpg 2x" data-file-width="459" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UKIP_poster_in_Alexandra_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1362476.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UKIP poster in <a href="/wiki/Egham" title="Egham">Egham</a>, Surrey, for the 2009 European elections</div></div></div>
<p>With regard to education policy, UKIP supports selective education through the creation of additional <a href="/wiki/Grammar_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammar schools">grammar schools</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015146_187-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETournier-Sol2015146-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> In its 2015 manifesto, UKIP promised to teach a chronological understanding of "British history and achievements" in schools,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayton2016403_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayton2016403-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> and it calls for the scrapping of <a href="/wiki/Sex_education" title="Sex education">sex education</a> for children under 11.<sup id="cite_ref-Education_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Education-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> UKIP would introduce an option for students to take an apprenticeship qualification instead of four non-core <a href="/wiki/General_Certificate_of_Secondary_Education" title="General Certificate of Secondary Education">GCSEs</a> which can be continued at <a href="/wiki/GCE_Advanced_Level" title="GCE Advanced Level">A Level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Education_237-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Education-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Schools would be investigated by <a href="/wiki/OFSTED" class="mw-redirect" title="OFSTED">OFSTED</a> on the presentation of a petition to the Department for Education signed by 25% of parents or governors.<sup id="cite_ref-Education_237-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Education-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> UKIP have promoted the scrapping of the government target that 50% of school leavers attend university, and present the policy that <a href="/wiki/Tuition_fees" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuition fees">tuition fees</a> would be scrapped for students taking approved degrees in science, medicine, technology, engineering or mathematics.<sup id="cite_ref-Education_237-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Education-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, it <a href="/wiki/Antidisestablishmentarianism" title="Antidisestablishmentarianism">opposed disestablishment</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> and said it would consider a transfer of part of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Estate" title="Crown Estate">Crown Estate</a> back to the Monarchy, in exchange for an end to annual state support.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Constitution_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Constitution-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Farage has argued that <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a> like <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> should have representatives in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons of the United Kingdom</a>, akin to the privileges given to French overseas territories in France. Farage believes that all citizens for whom the British Parliament passes legislation, whether in the United Kingdom or its territories, deserve democratic representation in that Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Support">Support</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_backing">Financial backing</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UKIP_campaigning_in_Newport_High_Street.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/UKIP_campaigning_in_Newport_High_Street.jpg/220px-UKIP_campaigning_in_Newport_High_Street.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/UKIP_campaigning_in_Newport_High_Street.jpg/330px-UKIP_campaigning_in_Newport_High_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/UKIP_campaigning_in_Newport_High_Street.jpg/440px-UKIP_campaigning_in_Newport_High_Street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1936" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UKIP_campaigning_in_Newport_High_Street.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A UKIP candidate campaigning in <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Isle_of_Wight" title="Newport, Isle of Wight">Newport</a> high street on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a>, 2012</div></div></div>
<p>In 2008, Usherwood noted that UKIP relied heavily on a small number of major financial backers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2008261_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2008261-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> According to <i>The Guardian</i>, a leaked internal report to UKIP's executive committee dated to September 2012 shows that the party's leader argued that "the key to money for us will be the <a href="/wiki/Hedge_fund" title="Hedge fund">hedge fund</a> industry".<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to UKIP's annual returns to the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> in 2013 the party had a total income of £2,479,314. Of this, £714,492 was from membership and subscriptions, £32,115 from fundraising activities and £1,361,640 from donations. By law, individual donations over £7,500 must be reported.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UKIP has several high-profile backers. In March 2009, the Conservative Party's biggest-ever donor, Stuart Wheeler, donated £100,000 to UKIP after criticising Cameron's stance towards the Treaty of Lisbon. He was then expelled from the Conservatives and in 2011 appointed treasurer of UKIP.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> In October 2014, <a href="/wiki/Arron_Banks" title="Arron Banks">Arron Banks</a>, who previously gave £25,000 to the Conservatives, increased his UKIP donation from £100,000 to £1 million after Hague said he had never heard of him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015151–152_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo2015151–152-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Halliday_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halliday-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> The multi-millionaire <a href="/wiki/Paul_Sykes_(businessman)" title="Paul Sykes (businessman)">Paul Sykes</a> has helped finance the party, donating over £1 million to their 2014 campaign at the European Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201537_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201537-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2014, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Desmond" title="Richard Desmond">Richard Desmond</a>, proprietor of <a href="/wiki/Express_Newspapers" class="mw-redirect" title="Express Newspapers">Express Newspapers</a>, donated £300,000 to UKIP.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016178_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016178-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Desmond had previously made the UKIP peer <a href="/wiki/David_Stevens,_Baron_Stevens_of_Ludgate" title="David Stevens, Baron Stevens of Ludgate">David Stevens</a> his deputy chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016183_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016183-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Halliday_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Halliday-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> The donation indicated that Desmond's papers, the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Express" title="Daily Express">Daily Express</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday Express">Sunday Express</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Star_(British_newspaper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily Star (British newspaper)">Daily Star</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Star_Sunday" title="Daily Star Sunday">Daily Star Sunday</a></i>, would back UKIP in the 2015 general election.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Three weeks before the election, Desmond gave the party a further £1&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016178_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeaconWring2016178-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2016, the major UKIP donor, Arron Banks, said that UKIP would be "dead in the water" if <a href="/wiki/Diane_James" title="Diane James">Diane James</a> did not become leader.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Following her departure after 18 days, Banks said that he would leave UKIP if <a href="/wiki/Steven_Woolfe" title="Steven Woolfe">Steven Woolfe</a> was prevented from running for leader, and if two other members remained in the party: "If <a href="/wiki/Neil_Hamilton_(politician)" title="Neil Hamilton (politician)">Neil Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Carswell" title="Douglas Carswell">Douglas Carswell</a> [UKIP's only MP] remain in the party, and the NEC decide that Steven Woolfe cannot run for leader, I will be leaving Ukip".<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership">Membership</span></h3>
<p>UKIP's membership numbers increased from 2002 to the time of the 2004 European Parliament election, before hovering around the 16,000 mark during the late 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC3May13_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC3May13-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-brief_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brief-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, the party claimed 20,000 members, with this remaining broadly stable, and in June 2007 it had a recorded 16,700 members.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbediLundberg200980_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbediLundberg200980-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> By July 2013, the figure had grown to 30,000<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> before ending the year at 32,447.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, the number was 36,000 on 22 April,<sup id="cite_ref-ExpressApril22_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExpressApril22-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> by 7 May reached 37,000<sup id="cite_ref-ExpressMay7_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExpressMay7-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> and on 19 May, less than a fortnight later and only three days before the 2014 European Parliament election, rose to 38,000.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> In January 2015, UKIP membership was the fifth highest of British parties.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_15_January_2015_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_15_January_2015-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Membership was 45,000 in May 2015, but since then has fallen to 32,757 in November 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> and as low as 18,000 under Henry Bolton by January 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2018, four political activists known through social media - <a href="/wiki/Paul_Joseph_Watson" title="Paul Joseph Watson">Paul Joseph Watson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Meechan" title="Mark Meechan">Mark Meechan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Benjamin" title="Carl Benjamin">Carl Benjamin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milo_Yiannopoulos" title="Milo Yiannopoulos">Milo Yiannopoulos</a> - joined the party. This was followed by the party gaining around five hundred members.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2018, it was reported the party attracted 3,200 new members in July, a 15% increase.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voter_base">Voter base</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25em;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r887775652"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">UKIP's voters are not single-issue Europhobes or political protesters, they share a clear and distinct agenda, mixing deep Euroscepticism with clear ideas about immigration, national identity and the way British society is changing. The conflict between UKIP's voters and the political mainstream reflects a deep-seated difference in outlook among voters from different walks in life. Those who lead and staff the three main parties are all from the highly educated, socially liberal middle classes, who are comfortable in an ethnically and culturally diverse, outward looking society... Those who lead and staff UKIP, and those who vote for them, are older, less educated, disadvantaged and economically insecure Britons, who are profoundly uncomfortable in the 'new' society, which they regard as alien and threatening.</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— Political scientists Robert Ford and Matthew Goodwin, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin201411_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin201411-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>In its early years, UKIP targeted itself toward southern English, middle-class Eurosceptic voters, those who had been supporters of the Conservative Party until <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a>'s Conservative government signed the Maastricht Treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014108_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014108-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> This led to the widespread perception that UKIP's supporters were primarily middle-class ex-Conservative voters, with commentator <a href="/wiki/Peter_Oborne" title="Peter Oborne">Peter Oborne</a> characterising UKIP as "the Conservative Party in exile".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014145_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014145-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After 2009, UKIP refocused its attention to appeal primarily to <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">white British</a>, working-class, blue-collar workers; those who had traditionally voted Labour or in some cases for Thatcher's Conservatives but who had ceased voting or begun to vote BNP since the emergence of the <a href="/wiki/New_Labour" title="New Labour">New Labour</a> project in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014108_266-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014108-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> In this way, UKIP's support base does not line up with the historical left-right divide in British politics, instead being primarily rooted in class divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014270_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014270-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> This mirrored the voting base of other radical right parties across Western Europe which had grown since the early 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014111–112_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014111–112-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> This scenario had come about following the rapid growth of the middle-classes and the concomitant decline of the working-class population in Western Europe; the centre-left, social-democratic parties who had traditionally courted the support of the working classes largely switched their attention to the newly emergent middle-classes, leaving their initial support base increasingly alienated and creating the vacuum which the radical right exploited.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014113–114_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014113–114-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the basis of their extensive study of data on the subject, in 2014 the political scientists <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Goodwin" title="Matthew Goodwin">Matthew Goodwin</a> and Robert Ford concluded that "UKIP's support has a very clear social profile, more so than any of the mainstream parties. Their electoral base is old, male, working class, white and less educated".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014159_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014159-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> They found that 57% of professed UKIP supporters were over the age of 54, while only one in ten were under 35, which they attributed to the fact that UKIP's socially conservative and Eurosceptic platform appealed far more to Britain's older generations that their younger counterparts, who were more socially liberal and less antagonistic toward the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014156–158_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014156–158-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>57% of UKIP supporters were male, which Ford and Goodwin suggested was due to women voters being put off by a number of high-profile <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">sexist</a> remarks made by UKIP candidates.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014154–155_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014154–155-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> 99.6% of UKIP supporters identified as white, reflecting the fact that ethnic minorities tended to avoid the party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014158–159_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014158–159-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> 55% of UKIP supporters had left school aged 16 or under, with only 24% having attended university, suggesting that the party primarily appealed to the least educated voters in society.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014154_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014154-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> Ford and Goodwin also found that UKIP's support base was more working-class than that of any other party, with 42% of supporters in <a href="/wiki/Blue-collar" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue-collar">blue-collar</a> jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014152_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014152-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Ford and Goodwin described UKIP's voters as primarily comprising the "left behind" sector of society, "older, less skilled and less well educated working-class voters" who felt disenfranchised from the mainstream political parties which had increasingly focused on attracting the support of middle-class <a href="/wiki/Swing_voters" class="mw-redirect" title="Swing voters">swing voters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin201410_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin201410-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ford and Goodwin nevertheless noted that UKIP was "not a purely blue-collar party but an alliance of manual workers, employers and the self-employed."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2016482_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2016482-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>
Geoffrey Evans and Jon Mellon highlighted that UKIP receive "a greater proportion of their support from lower professionals and managers" than from any other class group.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvansMellon2016474_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvansMellon2016474-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> They highlighted that polls repeatedly demonstrated that UKIP drew more votes from Conservative voters than Labour ones.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvansMellon2016464–465_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvansMellon2016464–465-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> They suggested that the assumption that working-class voters who supported UKIP had previously been Labour voters was misplaced,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvansMellon2016465_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvansMellon2016465-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> suggesting that these people had ceased voting for Labour "a long time before UKIP were an effective political presence", having been alienated by Labour's "pro-middle class, pro-EU and, as it eventually turned out, pro-immigration agenda".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvansMellon2016467_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvansMellon2016467-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>
In 2011, Goodwin, Ford, and David Cutts published a study that identified Euroscepticism as the main causal factor for voters supporting UKIP, with concern over immigration levels and distrust of the political establishment also featuring as important motives.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwinCutts2011204_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwinCutts2011204-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> They noted, however, that during elections for the European Parliament, UKIP was able to broaden its support to gain the vote of largely middle-class Eurosceptics who vote Conservative in other elections.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014231_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014231-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:25em;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r887775652"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">Ukip has become more than the single issue on which it was founded: under Farage's leadership it has become a welcoming home for the many in British society who feel that 'the system' isn't working for them, or has left them behind, economically, socially or politically. In so doing, it has gained supporters from across the political spectrum, including many old Labour voters in economically distressed regions of the country.</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— Political scientist Simon Usherwood, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2016a29_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUsherwood2016a29-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>From their analysis of the data, Ford and Goodwin stated that UKIP's support base has "strong parallels" both with that of Western Europe's other radical right parties and with the BNP during their electoral heyday.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014273_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014273-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> Conversely, an earlier study by Richard Whitaker and Philip Lynch, based on polling data from <a href="/wiki/YouGov" title="YouGov">YouGov</a>, concluded that UKIP voters were distinct from those of far-right parties. The authors found that voter support for UKIP correlated with concerns about the value of immigration and a lack of trust in the political system, but the biggest explanatory factor for their support of UKIP was Euroscepticism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhitakerLynch2011359_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhitakerLynch2011359-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> A further study by the same authors suggests that UKIP voters' core beliefs align very closely to those of the UKIP candidates; particularly so on issues surrounding European integration, which has resulted in Conservative voters switching to UKIP due to Conservative divisions on this issue.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynchWhitakerLoomes2012_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynchWhitakerLoomes2012-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> One study found that 63% of UKIP voters considered themselves to be right-wing, while 22% thought centrist and 16% thought leftist.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201592_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201592-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> 81% believed that immigration undermined British culture, a view shared by only half the wider British population.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201589–90_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201589–90-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> On economic issues, there was a divide between UKIP voters and the party itself.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201593_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201593-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> In contrast to the party's economic liberalism, UKIP supporters often held more leftist attitudes to the economy, with almost 80% opining that <a href="/wiki/Big_business" title="Big business">big business</a> took advantage of working people and almost 70% thinking that privatisation had gone too far.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201594_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201594-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UKIP has been most successful along England's eastern and southern coasts, in parts of south-west England, and in the Labour heartlands of Northern England and Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201573_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201573-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> It has not done well in London and in <a href="/wiki/University_town" class="mw-redirect" title="University town">university towns</a> and urban areas with younger populations like Oxford, Cambridge, Manchester, and Brighton.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201573,_74–75_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201573,_74–75-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> It has done well in areas with large numbers of old, white, and poorer people, and weaker in areas with larger numbers of younger, more ethnically and culturally diverse, and financially secure people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201573_292-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwinMilazzo201573-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>
Ford and Goodwin noted that UKIP "barely registers" with young Britons, graduates, ethnic minorities, and <a href="/wiki/Pro-EU" class="mw-redirect" title="Pro-EU">pro-EU</a> voters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014256_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFordGoodwin2014256-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup>
According to an Opinium poll in December 2014 on the views of 17- to 22-year-olds, Farage was the least popular political leader. Only 3% of young people questioned said that they intended to vote for UKIP, compared with 19% among voters of all ages.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> The 17% who said they would vote outside the three main parties were four times more likely to vote for the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party</a> than for UKIP.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> Conversely, a March 2015 <a href="/wiki/Ipsos_Mori" class="mw-redirect" title="Ipsos Mori">Ipsos Mori</a> poll found among 18- to 34-year-olds UKIP was polling nearly as well as the Green Party, somewhat contradicting the idea that Farage lacked appeal for younger voters.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> On the basis of their fieldwork among supporters of the <a href="/wiki/English_Defence_League" title="English Defence League">English Defence League</a> (EDL), an anti-Islam social movement, Winlow, Hall, and Treadwell noted that most EDL supporters whom they encountered intended to vote for UKIP in the build-up to the 2015 general election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinlowHallTreadwell201776_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinlowHallTreadwell201776-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UKIP supporters are sometimes nicknamed "kippers". In May 2017, in response to large defections from the party, Goodwin said "Former Kippers did not walk but literally sprinted over to the Conservatives."<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation">Organisation</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spokespersons">Spokespersons</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/UKIP_Frontbench_Team" title="UKIP Frontbench Team">UKIP Frontbench Team</a></div>
<p>The front bench team is divided into departmental sub-units, the principal ones being the economy, foreign policy and immigration. Sometimes the front bench team consists of more than just the principal positions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span></h3>
<p>UKIP's organisation is divided into twelve regions: London, South East, South West, Eastern, East Midlands, West Midlands, Yorkshire, North East, North West, Wales, Northern Ireland, and Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> An additional, thirteenth branch, operates in the <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>; it held its first public meeting at the Lord Nelson pub in April 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the end of 2013 the UKIP Scotland was dissolved after infighting tore the regional party apart; the party's administrative body was dissolved, Mike Scott-Hayward (the chairman and chief fundraiser) quit, and Farage fired Lord <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Monckton" class="mw-redirect" title="Christopher Monckton">Christopher Monckton</a> via email.<sup id="cite_ref-wipeout_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wipeout-304">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> The national party and UKIP Scotland focused on supporting the candidates for the upcoming European elections.<sup id="cite_ref-wipeout_304-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wipeout-304">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup>  After <a href="/wiki/David_Coburn_(politician)" title="David Coburn (politician)">David Coburn</a> won the seat, he was elected as leader of UKIP Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>
Veteran and former long-serving Antrim and Newtownabbey-based councillor, Robert Hill was appointed by Gerard Batten as UKIP's Spokesman for Northern Ireland in May 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> In August 2018, Welsh Assembly Member <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Bennett_(politician)" title="Gareth Bennett (politician)">Gareth Bennett</a> was elected as leader of UKIP in Wales after a membership ballot.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Representatives">Representatives</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party_representation_and_election_results" title="UK Independence Party representation and election results">UK Independence Party representation and election results</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Commons">House of Commons</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:365px;max-width:365px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_Carswell.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Douglas_Carswell.jpg/150px-Douglas_Carswell.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="209"
